NOOSE ENCIRCLES
NECK OF MINER
Cool CouesÂ»1 Averts a
Lynching in Shasta
County.
Men of Kennett Attempt to
Summarily Punish a
Wife-Beater.
Special Dispatch to The Call.
REDDING. June 9.â That there was not'
a lynching at the Shasta King mine of
the Trinity Copper Company, near Ken
nett, on Saturday afternoon was due less
to the tearful appeals of the victim than
to the sober intercession at a critical mo
ment of men whose advice was listened
to. by the half-frantic mob of miners. The
man who almost paid the death penalty
for his inhuman cruelty was a wife
beater. . Â¦- Â¦-.-Â¦;Â»;..
Some months ago a. miner named Fidler
went to the Shasta King to work. He was
accompanied by his wife and his 10-year
old daughter. They occupied a cabin near
the mouth of the main tunnel. Occasion
ally Fidler has been getting intoxicated,
and when in that condition he was said
to be very abusive to his wife and daugh
ter. Fidler was intoxicated on Saturday
when he went to his home. His wife and
daughter were heard to cry out, and pres
ently the little girl ran out screaming.
Her face was bleeding where the brutal
father had struck her. Fidler was then
engaged In inflicting punishment upon
his wife. He Is said to have beaten and
bruised her severely.
Word was passed up to the mine and a
crowd of Infuriated miners gathered. A
miner who is in Redding to-night declares
that the mob booted the brutal husband
into his sober senses and then some onÂ»
produced a rope. A slip noose was made,
thrown over Fldler's head and drawn,
snug about his throat. He prayed ana
begged to be spared.
Two or three cool-headed men came
upon the scene at this moment and so
earnestly counseled the leaders to hesitate
that they finally let the trembling miner
go with a threat. He probably will get
out of the county.
TWO MEN ABE ftTT.LFJ)
IN A LIGHTNING STORE!
Several Dwellings Are Badly Dam-
aged and the Property losses
Will Be Considerable.
COLUMBUS. Ga., June 9.â A heavy
wind and thunder storm passed over this
city last night, causing the death of two
men, perhaps fatally injuring a third and
doing considerable damage to property.
The dead: â¢ â¢ '
J. J. WILLIS, carpenter.
LOUIS McLAIN.
The injured: M. C. Cochran.
Willis was struck by lightning while
standing under a tree in company with
Cochran. The same bolt killed McLain.
who was Just across the river in Phoenix
City.
Several dwellings were struck by light
ning or unroofed by the storm.
Lightning Strikes Crowded Building.
ST. JOSEPH. Mo., June 9.â During: tha
graduation exercises of the Odell (Nebr.)
High School at the First Methodist
Church lightning struck the edifice, de
molishing a tower and rendering: several
spectators and graduates unconscious.
The building was soon anre and the lives
of many people were in peril. A largo
tank of water afforded prompt and effect
ive means of extinguishing the flames.
It Is believed no deaths will result, al
though several women were removed from
the church to their homes, suffering se
verely from shock. Â¦Â¦>r-\

Notice to Passengers.
Mrs. Herman Heyde, residing, at 11
Chapultepec street, reported yesterday
morning to Deputy Coroner McCormlck
the dlsappearnce of Herman Heyde, her
husband. He left home on February 19
with 5100 to go to Point .Richmond where
ho had secured employment as a carpen
ter, and was In company of two men, one
of whom he had met in an employment
office on Clay street. A- friend had re
ceived a postal card from him dated
Point Richmond, February 24, and that
was the last that his family has heard of
him. Several letters from his wife and
addressed to him at that place have been
returned to her unopened.

A Grand Opportunity.
As It was expected that several Eastern
crooks would take a trip to this city to
try their luck with the Shriners, Captain
Martin put his men to watching all the"
Incoming trains. So far none of the crodk
fraternity from the East has been dis
covered, but the watch will be kept up
till all the trains with the Shriners arrive.
It was not long before Detectives Crock
ett and RIordan brought in Charles Gagus
and Frank Wilson, well known bunko
men, and locked them up in the tanks.
Later Harry Walters and "Dick" Wilson
were brought in.
In view of the influx, of the Mystic
Shriners, Captain Martin- issued instruc
tions to the detectives yesterday morn
ing to bring in all known; pickpockets,
bunko men and other crooks, so that they
might be kept in durance vile till the
Shriners took their departure.

Lyons testified in his own behalf that
Conway on March 22 called upon him at
the County Clerk's office and asked him
to cash the order at the treasury as ,a
matter of convenience to a friend. Lyons,
on observing that the order was made
payable to. him, asked Conway for an ex
planation, and- Conway replied that as
Lyons was known to Cashier Perkins the
money would be promptly paid, but if
Cc'nway presented the order with hi3 own
name Perkins would think he was "graft
ing."*. In the. full, confidence that the of
der was genuine : and the transaction reg
ular Lyons presented: the order, received
the $250 and paid' if over to Conway in
Iront of Judge Graham's court. The in
ciaent passed out of his mind till Evans
called upon him on May 27 and asked him
v, hy he had withdrawn the bail money.
In cross-examination Lyons said he had
never spoken to Conway about the mat
ter till the night of May 27, when he met
him in a saloon at-Halght and Fillmore
streets with County Clerk Mahony and
others. At that time Conway showed a
Â¦receipt without- date from-Evans for the
$2M and remarked that it made him all
right. Lyons asked Conway why the re
ceipt had been made out in his name, and
Conway did â¢ not reply. He had known
Conway for five or six years and had
every, confidence in him. ,
The Judge, in dismissing the case, re
viewed the testimony and said that In
view of the testimony of Mr. Perkins that
it was customary for some of the Judges
to make their treasury . orders, payable
to persons other than the persons deposit-
ing the money there was nothing in the
mere circumstance of Lyons' name being
mentioned as the payee in the order calcu
lated to. even arouse Lyons' suspicion that
the transaction was irregular, much less
criminal. The Judge added that he had
little, if any, sympathy for Lyons in his
present dilemma, as he had admittedly
suffered his complaisant disposition arid
desire to accommodate Conway to impli
cate him in an embarrassing way in a
seemingly -crooked transaction. Whether
Errand larceny was the proper charge
against Conway and Lyons was a mat
ter, tn his judgment, worthy of serious
consideration, but he was not prepared at
that time to pass definitely upon It.
Cohway's case was continued till Fri
day. â¢

No applicant shall be privileged to take the
examinations unless he be the holder of a
valid teacher's certificate of a grade not lower
than the grammar grade.
Both the written and oral competitive ex
aminations shall .be marked on the scale of
100 credits each, thus making 200 credits for a
perfect standard. All the applicants shall be
arranged on a list In the order of their com
bined standing in both examinations. The
board shall determine the number which are
required ' for substitute duty and take such
number from the list of those examined in, the
order of their standing.
All assistants in primary and grammar
schools shall be appointed from a classified list
of such persons as shall successfully pass the
examinations. No person shall be appointed to
the eligible list without full and Impartial ex
amination of his or her qualifications and com
parison with the qualifications of all other per
sons whose names have come^before the board
as available for such appointment. No mem
ber of the Board of Education shall promise
or give any sort of assurance that any given
individual will be appointed to the* eligible
list or that any given, individual shall receive
his or her vote for such appointment. When
any name is placed on the eligible list record
shall be made of i any special qualification
which the person designated may possess and
of the kind or grade of work for which he
or she is specially suited.
APPOINTED FROM LIST.
Fifth â The next oral competitive examina
tion shall be held at the rooms of the Board
of Education Wednesday, July 9, at 0 a. m.
All' persons desiring -to enter the examina
tions except those who have done so since Au
gust 15. 1001, shall furnish the Board of Edu
cation at least ten days "prior to the time of
the competitive examination full information
relative to their " academic preparation, their
professional training (if any), and their ex
perience in teaching (if any). All- applicants
shall give not less than three nor more than
seven references to persons who are competent
to speak of their fitness for the work of
teaching-. Such references shall include the
persons whose present or former positions en
able them to give most exact and pertinent
information with reference to the applicant's
scholarship, training, and general
character and efficiency. The Board of Educa
tion will not consider general letters of recom
mendation; but they will request from the
persons referred to by applicant a confidential
statement as to the applicant's qualifications,
Buch statement to be given in answer to a
uniform list of questions to be furnished by
the board; . The board will also, in case of
doubt, call for and make use of . supplementary
information relating to the same, set of ques
tions from other persons who may bÂ« deemed
competent to speak intelligently of the can
didate's qualifications, j
